She has over two decades of experience starting at seed stage and staying involved for many years beyond.<\/em><\/h5>\n<h5 style=\"text-align: center;\"><em><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/allegra_v2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-mrf-link=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/allegra_v2\"><strong>Allegra Simon<\/strong><\/a>\u00a0loves working closely with incredible early-stage founders, cultivating the Cowboy community, and wearing many different hats as Chief of Staff to keep the Cowboy ranch thriving. She works closely with Aileen on new venture diligence, portfolio support, and everything else.<\/em><\/h5>\n<hr \/>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">It\u2019s been a decade<\/span> since publishing \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/11\/02\/welcome-to-the-unicorn-club\/\">Welcome to the Unicorn Club<\/a>,\u201d so it\u2019s a good time to reflect on what\u2019s happened since.<\/p>\n<p>In 2013, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cowboy.vc\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cowboy Ventures<\/a> had just gotten started. To inform our investment strategy, we assembled and studied a dataset of U.S.-based, VC-backed startups that had grown to be worth more than $1 billion within 10 years, using the term \u201cunicorn\u201d as a shorthand to capture how magical these companies seemed.<strong>\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653757\" style=\"width: 1370px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653757\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653757 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp\" alt=\"\" width=\"1360\" height=\"1020\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp 1360w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp?resize=150,113 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp?resize=300,225 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp?resize=768,576 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp?resize=680,510 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp?resize=1200,900 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-1-2013-unicorn-club.webp?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1360px) 100vw, 1360px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653757\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The most successful VC-backed U.S. tech companies less than 10 years old in 2013. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Our <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/11\/02\/welcome-to-the-unicorn-club\/\">original analysis<\/a> found only 39 unicorns out of the thousands of startups that had been founded by then. Some highlights:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li>The majority (62%) had gone public or been acquired.<\/li>\n<li>The majority were consumer-oriented: around 60% of companies, making up 80% of the value.<\/li>\n<li>Enterprise-oriented companies had 26x capital efficiency (current valuation divided by private capital raised), which was 2.4x better than consumer companies.<\/li>\n<li>One company became a \u201csuperunicorn\u201d (worth more than $100 billion) in that decade: Facebook.<\/li>\n<li>Contrary to the prevailing stereotype, the average age of a unicorn\u2019s founder was 34; it was 38 for enterprise software companies.<\/li>\n<li>The vast majority of companies had three co-founders and common work, school and tech experience.<\/li>\n<li>The Bay Area was HQ to 70% of unicorns. New York, home to three, was the second-largest hub.<\/li>\n<li>There was very little diversity: no female CEOs, and just 5% of unicorns had a female co-founder.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<h2>2013 to 2021: A rising tide for VC funds, startups and valuations<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653759\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653759\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653759 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"782\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png 2445w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=150,114 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=300,229 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=768,586 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=680,519 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=1536,1172 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=2048,1563 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=1200,916 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-2-VC-Capital-Raised-and-10-Year-Treasury-Yield.png?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653759\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Capital in the VC ecosystem tripled in a decade. Source: NVCA Q3 2023 VC Monitor, NVCA 2022 Yearbook, Federal Reserve Economic Data. \u00a0<strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Historical returns, growing markets (including social, mobile, cloud, commerce security, crypto and AI), COVID-era effects and <em>low<\/em> interest rates drove 3x more capital ($580 billion more!) into VC funds between 2013 and 2021 (and increased VC fee income by more than $11 billion).<\/p>\n<p>This enabled established VC firms to raise <a href=\"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/truebridge\/2022\/06\/14\/state-of-vc-2021-breaking-every-record\/?sh=5fc412c5fbe1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">record-breaking funds<\/a>; public \u201ccrossover\u201d funds joined the party; and <a href=\"https:\/\/files.pitchbook.com\/website\/files\/pdf\/Q2_2023_PitchBook_Analyst_Note_Challenges_for_Emerging_Managers.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">over a thousand newer firms <\/a>also raised funds. The industry gained thousands of new investors with fresh checkbooks and limited mentorship or oversight, given the pace.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>In 2021, it was a perfect storm of near-zero interest rates and much of the world spending their days behind screens, increasingly reliant on technology for work and life. Due-diligence processes were rushed, round sizes and valuations <a href=\"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/truebridge\/2022\/06\/14\/state-of-vc-2021-breaking-every-record\/?sh=5fc412c5fbe1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">broke records<\/a>, and a <em>huge<\/em> herd of unicorns was crowned.<\/p>\n<h2>The tide turns<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653760\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653760\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653760 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"762\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png 2523w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=150,112 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=300,223 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=768,572 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=680,506 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=1536,1143 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=2048,1524 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=1200,893 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-3-VC-Deal-vs-NASDAQ.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653760\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Investment in private companies mirrored the Nasdaq climb. Source: PitchBook-NVCA Venture Monitor, NVCA 2022 Yearbook, Federal Reserve Economic Data. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><strong>\u00a0<\/strong>In March 2022, the Fed raised rates, triggering a multiyear downward effect on public companies\u2019 revenue multiples and enterprise software firms\u2019 budgets. Although big VC firms continued to raise big money (64% of venture capital raised in 2022 went to funds <a href=\"https:\/\/pitchbook.com\/news\/articles\/venture-monitor-vc-trends-charts\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">bigger than $1 billion<\/a>), investors mostly froze their investments (around 40% of VCs <a href=\"https:\/\/pitchbook.com\/news\/articles\/active-VC-investors-decline\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stopped dealmaking<\/a> in 2023). Companies refocused on margins and profitability, cutting costs in several waves. Unicorns started to fall via down rounds, public delistings and shutdowns.<\/p>\n<p>But since 2013, there were 532 companies that joined the Unicorn Club. Similar to our original analysis, our 2023 dataset covers U.S.-based, VC-backed tech companies most recently valued at more than $1 billion in public or private markets and founded in 2013 or later.<\/p>\n<p>We use PitchBook, Crunchbase, People Data Labs, and news articles as sources but private market data is challenging. If you spot something inaccurate or we missed, please let us know at Cowboy Ventures.<\/p>\n<p>To note: Last-round valuations are an imperfect gauge, and they likely inflate the current herd size and value; <a href=\"https:\/\/www.fiercehealthcare.com\/health-tech\/online-mental-health-startup-cerebral-will-stop-prescribing-controlled-substances#:~:text=Kyle%20Robertson%2C%20a%20co%2Dfounder,for%20Robertson%20as%20Cerebral's%20CEO.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cerebral<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/04\/27\/clubhouse-needs-to-fix-things-and-today-it-cut-more-than-half-of-staff\/\">Clubhouse<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.theverge.com\/2023\/11\/3\/23945621\/opensea-2-0-starts-with-mass-layoffs-as-the-nft-balloon-deflates\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">OpenSea<\/a> may be good examples. Using the point-in-time methodology also leaves some companies out. For example, Stripe was founded in 2010, Zoom in 2011, and Snowflake and Coinbase in 2012. None of these was a unicorn in 2013 when we did the original analysis, and now they are more than 10 years old, so they\u2019ve been excluded from this dataset.<\/p>\n<p>Here\u2019s a brief look at our takeaways about the 532 companies in the 2023 Unicorn Club. Read on for a deeper dive into how things have changed over the last 10 years:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>The number of unicorns ballooned 14x in the past decade<\/strong>, from 39 to 532! They now serve a wider array of sectors (we\u2019re tracking 19), from climate and crypto to vertical SaaS.<\/li>\n<li><strong>The pendulum swung <em>hard<\/em> to<\/strong> <strong>enterprise<\/strong>, with 78% of unicorns today focused on B2B, the inverse of 2013.<\/li>\n<li><strong>Still, it\u2019s a wobbly, bloated herd <\/strong>that will thin in the coming years (likely to about 350) because \u2026\n<ul>\n<li>A whopping<strong> 93% are \u201cpapercorns\u201d:<\/strong> privately valued companies.<\/li>\n<li><strong>60% are \u201cZIRPicorns\u201d<\/strong>: Their last valuations were from 2020\u20132022, when interest rates were near zero, and many of these are running out of runway.<\/li>\n<li><strong>Around 20% of unicorns are on the cusp<\/strong>, valued at just about $1 billion.<\/li>\n<li><strong>Around 40% are trading at less than $1 billion<\/strong> in the secondary markets.<\/li>\n<li>BUT, there is lots of substance in this herd. And we see evidence of a <strong>Software<\/strong> <strong>Unicorn<\/strong> <strong>Power<\/strong> <strong>Law<\/strong>: The U.S. will be home to more than 1,000 unicorns by 2033.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<\/li>\n<li><strong>There have been very few exits.<\/strong>\u00a0Only 7% (35 companies) versus 66% a decade ago.<\/li>\n<li><strong>Capital efficiency declined <em>significantly.<\/em><\/strong>\u00a0This will be bad for exits, venture returns, founders and employees.<\/li>\n<li><strong>OpenAI will likely be the first superunicorn <\/strong>of the decade, and AI likely the mega-trend.<\/li>\n<li><strong>The Bay Area was home to more unicorns this time around but lost share<\/strong> as other hubs grew.<\/li>\n<li><strong>More unicorns means more founders,<\/strong> but some things didn\u2019t change at all.<\/li>\n<li><strong>Diversity is still wanted<\/strong>, and there\u2019s a lot of opportunity to improve the composition of founding teams.<\/li>\n<li><strong>If the past is a prologue,<\/strong> expect a mixed outlook for the current herd and many more unicorns in the future.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<h2>A deeper dive on where we are today<\/h2>\n<h3>Unicorns ballooned 14x in the past decade<\/h3>\n<p>This herd is worth a staggering <em>$1.5 trillion <\/em>in aggregate value (versus $260 billion in 2013). But becoming a unicorn is still not easily done: Less than 1% of VC-backed startups go on to become worth more than $1 billion. An ideal candidate is five times more likely to get into Stanford, Harvard or MIT than to found a unicorn.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653763\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653763\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653763 size-full\" style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"727\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=150,106 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=300,213 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=768,545 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=680,483 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=1536,1090 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=2048,1453 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=1200,852 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-4-Unicorns-Span-19-Categories.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653763\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Unicorns in 2023 innovate across an array of sectors. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.1px; font-size: 1rem;\">Unicorns now also span a wider array of sectors (we\u2019re tracking 19!). Most of these sectors weren\u2019t on our 2013 list (social, commerce and general enterprise dominated back then). Click the gallery <\/span>below<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.1px; font-size: 1rem;\"> to learn more about the most valuable companies in each sector.<\/span><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">\u00a0\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"google-slides-container\" style=\"position: relative; width: 100%; padding-top: 60%; overflow: hidden;\">\n<p><iframe class=\"embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%;\" src=\"https:\/\/docs.google.com\/presentation\/d\/e\/2PACX-1vSm8TBLWvA-WKV6oEX9UPKPyhkAkmYrvCjU5mwGzcdc1VOPH0203cFnjbtTzx9-VlLTkGtl3LIJkxYA\/embed?start=false&amp;loop=false&amp;delayms=60000\" width=\"100%\" height=\"100%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"><\/iframe><\/p>\n<\/div>\n<p><em>The most valuable companies are in very different sectors compared to 2013.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p>The most valuable unicorns in 2023 have innovated across a wide spectrum that stretches from general AI and healthcare to food delivery, HR software and stock trading. That marks a big departure from the sectors on the 2013 list. As previously noted, last-round valuation is an imperfect gauge: 75% of the \u201cunexited\u201d companies in this top 20 list were last valued in 2022 or earlier.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653764\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653764\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653764 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"750\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=150,110 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=300,220 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=768,562 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=680,498 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=1536,1124 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=2048,1499 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=1200,879 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-6-Founding-Years-of-2023-Unicorns.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653764\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Companies of all ages became unicorns in the run-up. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Unlike in our 2013 analysis, there were no <em>best<\/em> years for founding a unicorn: 2020 and 2021 accelerated the &#8220;crowning&#8221; of all ages and stages of companies. Today\u2019s unicorns are seven years old on average, same as a decade ago, which seems like a good thing.<\/p>\n<p>We don\u2019t analyze fallen unicorns here. But anecdotally, we see being crowned a unicorn too quickly could be a curse. Fallen unicorns like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/10\/hopin-raises-125m-for-its-online-events-platform-on-the-back-of-surging-growth\/\">Hopin<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/qz.com\/1305719\/electric-scooter-company-bird-is-the-fastest-startup-ever-to-become-a-unicorn\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bird<\/a> were crowned within one year of founding; car leaser <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2019\/12\/19\/softbank-fair-car-market-disruption\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fair<\/a> in two years; and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/09\/21\/on-demand-trucking-app-convoy-raises-185m-at-1b-valuation\/\">Convoy<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.builtinnyc.com\/2019\/08\/21\/knotel-reaches-unicorn-status-after-400m-round\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Knotel <\/a>just three years after founding.<\/p>\n<h2>The pendulum swung hard to enterprise<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653765\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653765\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653765 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"748\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=150,110 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=300,219 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=768,561 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=680,496 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=1536,1121 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=2048,1495 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=1200,876 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-7-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Enterprise-Companies.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653765\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Enterprise companies are worth $1.2 trillion, 80% of aggregate value. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Ten years ago, we found just 15 (38%) unicorns building B2B software and services comprising just $55 billion in total value. Workday, ServiceNow, Splunk and Palantir were the most valuable enterprise unicorns at the time.<\/p>\n<p>Today, there are 416 enterprise unicorns \u2014 making up around 78% of the list \u2014 worth <em>$1.2 trillion<\/em> and driving 80% of aggregate value (versus 20% in 2013).<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653766\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653766\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653766 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"736\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png 3600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=150,108 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=300,216 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=768,552 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=680,489 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=1536,1105 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=2048,1473 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=1200,863 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-8-2023_s-20-Highest-Valued-Consumer-Companies.png?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653766\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Consumer companies comprise 20% of our list. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Consumer companies today make up 20% of aggregate value, a big contrast to the 80% they accounted for back in 2013. Remember \u201cSoMoCo\u201d? Social (<a href=\"https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Facebook<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.pinterest.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Pinterest<\/a>), mobile (<a href=\"https:\/\/www.uber.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Uber<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/squareup.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Square<\/a>) and e-commerce (<a href=\"https:\/\/www.groupon.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Groupon<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.gilt.com\/boutique\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gilt<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/fabfitfun.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fab<\/a>).<\/p>\n<p>The most valuable consumer startups today operate in areas like last-mile delivery (DoorDash, Gopuff), health (Devoted, Ro, Cityblock), and gaming-driven platforms (Discord, Rec Room) \u2014 companies that drove new habits during COVID.<\/p>\n<p>What caused so much capital to flock to enterprise companies in the past decade? The attraction of historical capital efficiency, the predictability of SaaS business models (high gross margin and customer retention), and a growing number of highly valued potential acquirers were likely a big draw. Global adoption of cloud made it easier to adopt new software and opened a big window for a whole new ecosystem of application layer, infrastructure, data and analytics, and security companies.<\/p>\n<p>The cyclical pendulum does swing, so given the hard shift to enterprise, we hope and expect more exciting consumer unicorns will be born in coming years. For inspiration, many of today\u2019s leading consumer internet experiences are about two decades old (eBay, Expedia, OpenTable, Tripadvisor, StubHub, Yelp), possibly fertile territory?<\/p>\n<h2>A bloated herd<\/h2>\n<p>Our 532 companies are a wobbly, bloated herd that will thin in the coming years to around 350. That\u2019s because a whopping 93% of unicorns are actually \u201cpapercorns\u201d: privately valued on paper but not yet \u201cliquid.\u201d It\u2019s a big change from just 36% private unicorns in 2013.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653761\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653761\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653761 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"761\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png 2523w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=150,111 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=300,223 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=768,571 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=680,505 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=1536,1141 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=2048,1522 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=1200,892 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-9-Unicorns-Crowned-vs-10-Year-Treasury-Deal.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653761\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A spate of ZIRPicorns was crowned when rates troughed. Sources: PitchBook, Federal Reserve Economic Data. Note this includes all VC-backed companies valued at $1 billion for the first time in a given year, including those founded before 2013. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Sixty percent of unicorns today are what we call \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/07\/as-interest-rates-rise-startups-and-vcs-are-playing-a-new-game\/\">ZIRP<\/a>icorns\u201d: They were last valued between January 2020 and March 2022, which saw peak public multiples and near-zero interest rates.<\/p>\n<p>When money was flowing, unprofitable private companies were often able to raise enough to fund two to five years of operations. This means that operating runways are getting short for many unicorns. Many are working to get profitable on existing cash, which is challenging given the current economy and is even harder when starting with a lower gross margin business.<\/p>\n<p>Given the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2024\/01\/04\/vcs-predict-more-exits-in-2024\/\">chilly current M&amp;A environment<\/a>, founders\u2019 resistance to recapitalization, and investors\u2019 fear of \u201ccatching a falling knife\u201d by investing in a down round, we expect more abrupt shutdowns in 2024 (e.g., <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2023\/10\/19\/convoy-trucking-tech-startup-shuts-down-jeff-bezos-investor\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Convoy<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.healthcaredive.com\/news\/olive-ai-shuts-down\/698455\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Olive Health, <\/a><a href=\"https:\/\/www.axios.com\/2023\/06\/12\/softbank-pizza-robot-shuts-down-zume-445-million\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Zume<\/a>) (\u201cunicorpses,\u201d anyone?).<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653755\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653755\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653755 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"724\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=150,106 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=300,212 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=768,543 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=680,481 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=1536,1085 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=2048,1447 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=1200,848 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-10-Unicorn-Valuation-Distribution.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653755\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Valuations skew lower in this herd, and many are on the cusp of being a unicorn. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Coining the term also seems to have affected the market (sorry!): 21% are valued at $1 billion (versus 10% in 2013), on the cusp of being a \u201cunicorn,\u201d and 46% at less than $2 billion.<\/p>\n<p>Around 40% are trading below the $1 billion valuation mark in secondary markets, according to real order data for 290 unicorns on our list from <a href=\"https:\/\/www.hiive.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hiive<\/a>. It\u2019s possible more might trade at less than $1 billion.<\/p>\n<p>On the bright side, we see approximately 350 healthy businesses of substance in this herd \u2014 almost 10x in a decade! Many ZIRPicorns and papercorns raised enough capital and are successfully navigating the new climate, and will grow into and beyond their current valuations. Many will become public companies in the coming years, with rock-solid financials, tested by the downturn. And a few of these companies will grow to become superunicorns.<\/p>\n<p>And, we see evidence of a <strong>Software Unicorn Power Law<\/strong>.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653767\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653767\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653767 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"765\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=150,112 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=300,224 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=768,574 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=680,508 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=1536,1148 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=2048,1531 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=1200,897 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-11-Moore_s-law-1.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653767\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">An echo of Moore\u2019s law? Unicorn growth tracks compute power growth. Source: Our World In Data, plus PitchBook\u2019s list of total U.S.-based private unicorns (including those founded before 2013). Note this chart is for illustrative purposes. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The number of unicorns increased at an amazing 30% on average every year in the past decade, spurred by <a href=\"https:\/\/www.statista.com\/statistics\/203428\/total-enterprise-software-revenue-forecast\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">enterprise software spend<\/a>, consumer tech adoption, VC funding and interest rates.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2654047\" style=\"width: 886px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2654047\" class=\"breakout  wp-image-2654047\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/image-1.png?w=680\" alt=\"A chart comparing the size of unicorns\" width=\"876\" height=\"687\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2654047\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>We see an echo of Moore\u2019s law here: As compute capacity, capability and usage increase, the number of unicorns increases. The current momentum in AI should add fuel to innovation and demand.<\/p>\n<p>Adjusting the current herd to 350, future unicorn growth to a less bubbly 15%, and improving current capital efficiency a bit, we see 4x more, or about 1,400 U.S. unicorns, in 2033. Counterarguments to this line of thinking include scarcer venture capital, higher interest rates and software consolidation. But previous downturns have been fertile for unicorn founding. This will be exciting for the future of innovation, jobs and the tech economy, despite current conditions.<\/p>\n<h2>The exclusive \u201cliquid unicorn\u201d club<\/h2>\n<p>There have been few exits: only 7% versus 66% in the prior decade. Just 35 of 532 unicorns are public or were acquired for over $1 billion, a consequence of increased private capital and a more challenging regulatory and M&amp;A environment. The average time from founding to an IPO or acquisition was a speedy six years, and an impressive 75% of founding CEOs led their companies from founding through an exit.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653768\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653768\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653768 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"724\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=150,106 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=300,212 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=768,543 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=680,481 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=1536,1087 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=2048,1449 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=1200,849 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-13-The-Exclusive-Public-Unicorn-Club.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653768\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Just 14 of 532 unicorns are public today. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The public unicorn club is elite, with just 3% public compared to 41% going public the decade prior. That\u2019s a huge change, partly driven by the availability of so much private capital and investors willing to invest in richer-than-public valuations in the last decade.<\/p>\n<p>These companies are split between enterprise and consumer and span a wide array of sectors.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s also notable that around 70% of the current public unicorns\u2019 CEOs were the founding CEOs. So many leaders scaling from being a startup founder and individual contributor to leading and managing a multi-billion-dollar public company is impressive!<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653762\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653762\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653762 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"761\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png 2523w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=150,111 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=300,223 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=768,571 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=680,505 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=1536,1141 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=2048,1522 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=1200,892 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-14-Fallen-Unicorn-Market-Caps.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653762\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Just a sample of formicorns\u2019 struggle in public markets, many spurred by SPACs. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Reflecting the times, there are more fallen public unicorns than healthy public unicorns in this herd. At least 20 unicorns went public in the last decade, then fell below $1 billion in value (hello, SPACs), versus just 14 current public unicorns. (These, and companies previously valued at less than $1 billion but subsequently acquired or recapitalized at a lower valuation, are not included in our analysis.)<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653754\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653754\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653754 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"724\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=150,106 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=300,212 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=768,543 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=680,481 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=1536,1087 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=2048,1449 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=1200,849 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-15-Acquired-Unicorns.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653754\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A paltry 4% of 2023 unicorns had an \u201cexit\u201d via acquisition vs. 23% in 2013. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Just 21 companies were acquired, spanning a diverse set of sectors: Two-thirds were in enterprise and the rest consumer. The average acquisition price was $2.4 billion, about 2x that of 2013. Notably, 33% of these deals involved hardware companies (Cruise, Raxium, Ring, Zoox, etc.), likely a consequence of low interest rates for both unicorns and acquirers.<\/p>\n<h2>Capital efficiency declined significantly<\/h2>\n<p>Unicorn capital efficiency dropped significantly over the last 10 years \u2014 precipitously for enterprise companies. This will be bad for exits, venture returns, founders and employees.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653769\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653769\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653769 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"722\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=150,106 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=300,212 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=768,541 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=680,479 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=1536,1083 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=2048,1444 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=1200,846 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-16-Average-Capital-Efficiency-Valuation-_-Equity-Raised.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653769\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Capital efficiency plummeted among enterprise unicorns. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The most successful VC-backed tech companies have historically delivered outsized returns. Delivering a 26x return within 10 years is outstanding (about 40% IRR), but investors (and talent) have to risk years of illiquidity versus other asset classes or industries.<\/p>\n<p>In the past decade, tech has lost its capital efficiency edge. Enterprise companies\u2019 formerly impressive capital efficiency of 26x plummeted to 7x, putting it in line with consumer companies\u2019 efficiency (despite typically higher margins and customer retention), which also dropped from 11x to 7x. Given that many unicorns are currently overvalued, even 7x is likely inflated.<\/p>\n<p>In other words, investors would have been better off investing in public superunicorns like Salesforce, Amazon, and Microsoft (up 8x, 9x, and 9x, respectively) than in many companies in our current unicorn herd.<\/p>\n<p>Let\u2019s use an example to illustrate capital efficiency as we define it: current valuation divided by private capital raised.<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li>Let\u2019s say a company has raised $600 million in preferred stock rounds plus $100 million in debt.<\/li>\n<li>With strong customer traction and a magnetic CEO, in 2021 the company grows to run-rate revenue of $100 million and raises capital at a $3 billion valuation, mirroring the 30x multiples of high-growth public comparable companies.<\/li>\n<li>Employees get common options at 50% the preferred price \u2014 a $1.5 billion valuation.<\/li>\n<li>Then comes 2022. Churn skyrockets and new sales dry up. The company reduces its headcount from 1,000 to 500 over several waves of layoffs. The team fights like hell and gets back to $100 million ARR by 2025, and almost reaches breakeven.<\/li>\n<li>In 2025, the company is offered a $500 million acquisition offer by a private equity firm, or 5x its revenue, the current public market comparable.<\/li>\n<li>The management takes the deal, agreeing to an 8% &#8220;carveout&#8221; for themselves ($20 million) and employees ($20 millions) as stock options are \u201cunderwater.\u201d Debtors get paid in full, investors get about 60% of their investment back, and employees who stay with the company get about $30,000 at exit after four to 10 years of work.<\/li>\n<li>The company\u2019s capital efficiency is 0.83x ($500 million\/$600 million equity raised).<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p>Interest rates again had a big impact here: As rates fell, investors maintained confidence in historical venture returns, while competition grew for allocation in hot deals. This caused many to overlook valuations, business model margins, payback periods and burn rates as they invested.<\/p>\n<p>For the startup industry to once again deliver outsized returns, we have to regain capital efficiency discipline.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653770\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653770\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653770 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"829\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=150,121 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=300,243 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=768,621 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=680,550 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=1536,1243 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=2048,1657 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=1200,971 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-17-20-Most-Capital-Efficient-Companies.png?resize=50,40 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653770\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Shoutouts to highly capital efficient companies (with caveats). <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The above chart highlights highly capital-efficient companies, with caveats. The vast majority of these are \u201cpapercorns,\u201d so this list does not reflect realized capital efficiency. Cruise\u2019s efficiency is based on its $1 billion acquisition by GM in 2016 after being founded in 2014. The company has raised billions more since as a GM subsidiary, which paints a very different picture of its current efficiency.<\/p>\n<p>In our 2013 analysis, Workday and ServiceNow were standouts, with capital efficiency of 60x each. Their market caps are also 5x and 19x higher now, respectively.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653771\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653771\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653771 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"765\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=150,112 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=300,224 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=768,574 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=680,508 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=1536,1148 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=2048,1531 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=1200,897 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-18-Capital-Efficiency-by-Sector.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653771\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Some 2023 unicorns are currently worth\u00a0 &lt;2x capital raised. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>If you\u2019re looking for evidence that companies raised too much in the past decade, about 20% of companies on our list are worth less than 4x their capital raised. Given how many are likely overvalued, reality will likely be worse than this. The categories with the lowest average capital efficiency were climate\/energy, real estate, and healthcare.<\/p>\n<h2>OpenAI is likely to become the decade\u2019s superunicorn, and AI the megatrend<\/h2>\n<p>The previous major waves of tech innovation have each crowned a superunicorn that grows to be worth more than $100 billion over time, like Microsoft, Cisco, Amazon, and Meta. (Meta is the only one to be crowned within the last 10 years.)<\/p>\n<p>OpenAI is close to being the first AI superunicorn, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2023-12-22\/openai-in-talks-to-raise-new-funding-at-100-billion-valuation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">rumored<\/a> to be raising at a valuation of more than $100 billion, at just eight years old.<\/p>\n<p>At times over the past 10 years, crypto looked like it could be the mega-trend of the decade. Coinbase hit a market cap of $76 billion in November 2021 after going public months earlier; it\u2019s now worth about $32 billion (because Coinbase was founded in 2012, it is not included in this dataset).<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653774\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653774\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653774 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"724\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png 1600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png?resize=150,106 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png?resize=300,212 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png?resize=768,543 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png?resize=680,481 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png?resize=1536,1087 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png?resize=1200,849 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-19-super-unicorns.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653774\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Superunicorns grew superpowers, 2013\u20132023. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>There are now 15 VC-backed superunicorns, and they got a lot more valuable over the last decade. Meta was worth $122 billion in 2013 and is worth about $950 billion, or 8x, today.<\/p>\n<p>Superunicorns have superpowers that help create and\/or disrupt entire categories \u2014 like Netflix (worth more than Comcast, Paramount, and Warner Bros. combined) and Tesla (worth more than the next five largest public automakers combined).<\/p>\n<p>Of our original dataset, three more became superunicorns in recent years: ServiceNow, Uber, and Palo Alto Networks. And Airbnb is on the horizon at $88 billion. They\u2019ve grown to be worth more than Hyatt and Marriott combined and have the benefit of network effects.<\/p>\n<p>Superunicorn power may compound further in the coming years, with software consolidation and tighter capital constraints for smaller-scale players.<\/p>\n<h2>The herd spreads beyond the Bay<\/h2>\n<p>The Bay Area gained in numbers but lost ground as the home of unicorns as other hubs grew.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653775\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653775\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653775 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"932\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png 1600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png?resize=150,137 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png?resize=300,273 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png?resize=768,699 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png?resize=680,619 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png?resize=1536,1398 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png?resize=1200,1092 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-20-Unicorn-HQ.png?resize=50,46 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653775\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">COVID effects likely helped spread more unicorns across the country. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><strong>\u00a0<\/strong>The significance of geography continues to evolve, given COVID-era effects. Many unicorns are now spread across multiple cities and offer a hybrid work environment to employees. Notably, at least 22 have <a href=\"https:\/\/www.flex.scoopforwork.com\/about\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">no physical HQ office<\/a>, according to Flex Index data. But there are clear economic and local network effects to geographical unicorn hubs. Many CEOs cite productivity, creativity and cultural gains from in-person work, relevant for hopeful future unicorns.<\/p>\n<p>The Bay Area is still the largest unicorn pasture, but it lost a lot of ground, from being home to 69% of unicorns in 2013 to 45% in 2023. On the bright side, it\u2019s home to 238 unicorns (including the four most valuable: OpenAI, Databricks, DoorDash, and Samsara), 9x more than in 2013.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s unclear whether the Bay Area will regain its stature as unicorn central. A lot may depend on return-to-work policies, the importance and concentration of AI talent, and the quality and cost of living compared to other hubs, as well as the next generation of unicorns.<\/p>\n<p>New York\u2019s share grew a lot <em>(<\/em>11% to 19%) as the second-largest hub. The city is now home to 100 unicorns (about 40% are crypto\/web3 or fintech, including OpenSea and Chainalysis).<\/p>\n<p><strong>Many geographies grew from having no or few unicorns to becoming HQ to more than 10: <\/strong>Los Angeles (CloudKitchens, Blockdaemon); Boston (Devoted Health, Circle); Seattle (Auth0, Outreach); Austin (Everlywell, Workrise); Chicago (VillageMD, Tegus); and Denver (Guild, Crusoe).<\/p>\n<h2>More unicorns, more founders! But some things didn\u2019t change at all<\/h2>\n<p>More unicorns spread across more geographies, and founders now hail from a broader variety of backgrounds. Using publicly available information and data from <a href=\"https:\/\/www.peopledatalabs.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">People Data Labs<\/a>, our list grew to more than 1,300 founders versus around 100 in 2013.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653776\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653776\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653776 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"1281\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png 1279w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png?resize=120,150 120w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png?resize=240,300 240w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png?resize=768,961 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png?resize=544,680 544w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png?resize=1228,1536 1228w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png?resize=959,1200 959w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-21-co-founders-of-10-highest-valued-unicorns.png?resize=40,50 40w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653776\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Notice what most of these founders have in common? <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><strong>Eighty-three percent <\/strong>of unicorns in the last decade had co-founders (versus 90% in 2013). On average, companies had three co-founders \u2014 same as 10 years ago. The average age at founding was 35, one year older than 2013. Twenty-somethings and college dropouts are still outliers.<\/p>\n<p>About 70% of founders worked previously in tech, very similar to our 2013 data.<\/p>\n<p>Around 65% of founders went to school or worked together (a decrease from 90% in 2013), and 67% of teams have a co-founder with founder experience of some kind (versus 80%). Prior pursuits ranged from founding a small tutoring biz, to Jet.com and Twitch, to a fallen unicorn like WeWork.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653929\" style=\"width: 910px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653929\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653929\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/image.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"900\" height=\"826\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/image.png 611w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/image.png?resize=150,138 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/image.png?resize=300,275 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/image.png?resize=50,46 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653929\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>But founders\u2019 educational and work backgrounds are much more diverse today. Only about 20% of founders went to a \u201ctop 10 school\u201d (as defined by U.S. News &amp; World Report) compared to two-thirds in 2013. No school has more than 5% \u201cmarket share.\u201d Stanford still leads as the alma mater of 5%, but accounts for much less than the 33% it did in 2013.<\/p>\n<p>About 40% of co-founders are \u201cnon-technical\u201d by education, bucking the \u201cfounders must be technical\u201d stereotype. Twenty-five percent majored in business and 15% in the humanities, while 60% majored in a STEAM field. In 2013, 90% of CEOs had technical degrees, a big change. According to People Data Labs, just around a third of founders previously held software engineering roles.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653778\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653778\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653778 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"673\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png 1600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png?resize=150,99 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png?resize=300,197 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png?resize=768,505 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png?resize=680,447 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png?resize=1536,1010 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png?resize=1200,789 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-23-top-prior-employers.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653778\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Prior employers include superunicorns, banking, consulting and military. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>A surprisingly high 20% of co-founders previously worked at a superunicorn, likely tied to the fact that 70% of co-founders today have worked previously in tech. Google leads as the top breeding ground for unicorn founders: We found 87 with work experience at Google, which is about 6% of co-founders.<\/p>\n<h2>Diversity has lots of room for improvement<\/h2>\n<p>As unicorns proliferated, co-founders\u2019 geographies, education and work backgrounds did, too. This is exciting news for future founders.<\/p>\n<p>Improvement has been slow when it comes to co-founder gender diversity: Just 14% of unicorns now have a female co-founder (versus 5% in 2013), and 5% have a female founding CEO (compared to none in 2013).<\/p>\n<p>These numbers are still quite pathetic: There are more founders named Michael, David and Andrew than there are women CEOs of unicorns. At this rate, we won\u2019t reach equal gender representation until 2063.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2653779\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2653779\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2653779 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"641\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png 1600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png?resize=150,94 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png?resize=300,188 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png?resize=768,481 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png?resize=680,426 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png?resize=1536,962 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png?resize=1200,752 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/01\/Image-24-share-of-unicorns-with-female-founder.png?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2653779\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Some sectors have more gender diversity at the top vs. others. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cowboy Ventures<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s challenging to track other aspects of identity like race or whether the person is a member of the LGBTQ+ community. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.mckinsey.com\/featured-insights\/diversity-and-inclusion\/diversity-wins-how-inclusion-matters\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Myriad studies<\/a> show diverse teams deliver better results, including in <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2019\/12\/20\/diversity-inclusion-key-to-beating-next-recession\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">downturns<\/a>, so improving diversity given the tougher times seems like a no-brainer.<\/p>\n<p>Case in point: The elite public unicorn club has higher gender diversity at the top: 14% have female CEOs (two) and 21% have female co-founders (three).<\/p>\n<h2>Looking ahead: The next 10 years<\/h2>\n<p>If the past is a prologue, expect change ahead for this herd of unicorns and a very different, much larger list in 2033. Numbers, sectors, and founder backgrounds changed <em>so much<\/em> this past decade.<\/p>\n<p>Our original 39 had mixed fates. About half are currently public companies and around 80% are worth more today. Three more became superunicorns (ServiceNow, Palo Alto Networks and Uber), and network effect companies (we love network effects!) also grew stronger (Uber + Airbnb + LinkedIn = value of whole original list).<\/p>\n<p>Enterprise companies fared more reliably, increasing 6x in value since 2013. All but one (Rocket Fuel) maintained unicorn status through the second decade. So consumer companies had bumpier journeys. Thirty-three percent are smaller today (Lending Club, Yelp), and some have had fire sales or shut down (Tumblr, Zulily).<\/p>\n<p>The size, scale and number of VC firms will also change in the coming years. In 2013, there were about 850 active venture funds. Today there are about 2,500. As unicorns fall out of the dataset, we expect more <a href=\"https:\/\/pitchbook.com\/news\/articles\/VC-zombie-funds-consolidation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">change in VC firms<\/a>. Some VCs will retire, some will raise smaller funds (right-sized for better returns), downsize teams, or fold. Given the likelihood of lower returns from many papercorns in this herd, change seems inevitable. We\u2019ve seen \u201cVC musical chairs\u201d in previous cycles, and it\u2019s happening again.<\/p>\n<p>As noted in our <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/11\/02\/welcome-to-the-unicorn-club\/\">original post<\/a>, multi-billion-dollar VC funds need multi-billion-dollar outcomes to deliver acceptable returns. As funds got bigger, their incentives changed and drove round sizes and valuations higher, with some negative consequences. We don\u2019t expect VC firms to go back to 2013 in staff or AUM. But the lessons here should give founders, VCs and LPs lots of caution about too much money, too early and too fast \u2014 and from whom.<\/p>\n<p>That said, despite the sins of the past decade, technology continues to change our world. Founders have access to more inspiration, role models, capital and talent than ever. Unicorns are still relatively few and small versus the number of much larger, slower-moving companies with outdated technology. We see miles of green fields for more unicorns in years to come.<\/p>\n<h2>What does this all mean?<\/h2>\n<p>The march of technology has created so many more unicorns, serving a much wider array of sectors. Crunching the numbers, you can\u2019t help but reflect on the enormous societal and financial impact VC-backed tech has had and get excited for more history to unfold.<\/p>\n<p>It feels like we\u2019re living during a new Industrial Revolution, powered by software, that is starting to spread to more and more sectors of society. <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2021\/06\/04\/tech-companies-fortune-500-salesforce-benioff-carvana-brainstorm-podcast\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Less than 10%<\/a> of today\u2019s Fortune 500 companies are tech companies. In the next 10 years, we expect the share to rise \u2014 and many to be from the 2023 herd.<\/p>\n<p>We\u2019ve also learned indelible lessons. That macroeconomic factors and cycles matter. The massive influx of private capital caused a proliferation of companies but a decline in capital efficiency discipline, which will degrade financial outcomes for years, given how many are still papercorns.<\/p>\n<p>The cycle is far from over. The venture ecosystem will feel the impact of the past decade in years to come via more shutdowns, down rounds and scarred founders, employees and investors.<\/p>\n<p>Valuation is also clearly a convenient but imperfect, impermanent measure of success. Becoming a unicorn at a young age might even be a curse! Founders today can see how chasing vanity valuations with weak underlying fundamentals can lead to unintended poor outcomes.<\/p>\n<p>There were times in the decade when many believed building a unicorn was easy and common. Elder unicorns know that it\u2019s not. It requires the sustained magic of product and velocity, customer love, business model economics, capital efficiency, relentless execution and more, over many years.<\/p>\n<p>We tip our hats once again to the hundreds of companies (no longer tens!) that achieved and maintained unicorn milestones. Building and sustaining more than $1 billion in value in the past 10 years was statistically improbable and a major, special team effort.<\/p>\n<p>Finally, if you made it this far, thank you for taking the time to dive into our labor of love. We hope you enjoyed it. We\u2019d love comments on what you appreciated most, disagree with, what we missed, or what you\u2019d like more of.<\/p>\n<p><em>For more like this (although we promise other posts are shorter), reddit-ipo-again\/","title":{"rendered":"Counting down to the Reddit IPO (again)"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Reddit could finally<\/span> <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2024\/01\/18\/reddit-plans-to-launch-ipo-in-march-report-says\/\">go public this year<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>On the heels of <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/08\/circle-ipo-makes-sense\/\">Circle&#8217;s IPO filing<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2024\/01\/12\/tech-ipos-filings-nasdaq\/\">news from a major exchange<\/a> that a host of companies are preparing to go public this year, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/markets\/deals\/reddit-seeks-launch-ipo-march-sources-2024-01-18\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Reuters reports<\/a> that Reddit has &#8220;detailed plans&#8221; to go public in March.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><strong><em>The Exchange explores startups, markets and money. <\/em><\/strong><\/p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><strong><em>Read it <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/subscribe\/?tpcc=theexchange\">every morning on TechCrunch+<\/a> or get <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\/?utm_source=internal&amp;utm_medium=WPunit\">The Exchange newsletter<\/a> every Saturday.<\/em><\/strong><\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p>Now, before the rumor mill gets going, let&#8217;s make one thing clear: Reddit going public in the first quarter is not going to throw the IPO window wide open for other tech companies waiting to exit. Most <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2024\/01\/18\/welcome-back-to-the-unicorn-club-10-years-later\/\">unicorns in the market today<\/a> build products for other businesses, while Reddit is a more consumer-focused business that makes money from advertising and subscriptions. Still, if Reddit manages to pull off a strong IPO, it would help make going public palatable for companies of all sorts. An IPO at this time could stand to have a bigger impact if this were a B2B-focused company, but you can&#8217;t always get what you want.<\/p>\n<p>We may have a number of potentially big IPOs in the queue today. Besides Reddit and Circle, huge companies <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/06\/shein-reportedly-seeks-90-billion-valuation-in-ipo\/\">like Shein<\/a> are also reportedly busy getting their S-1 and F-1 ducks in a row. They represent a possible vanguard, but in reality, they don&#8217;t make up even a fraction of the number of companies that need to go public.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"dTmXZkIkvR\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2024\/01\/18\/reddit-plans-to-launch-ipo-in-march-report-says\/\">Reddit plans to launch IPO in March, report says<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Reddit plans to launch IPO in March, report says&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2024\/01\/18\/reddit-plans-to-launch-ipo-in-march-report-says\/embed\/#?secret=llH1AUCSJS#?secret=dTmXZkIkvR\" data-secret=\"dTmXZkIkvR\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Cowboy Ventures&#8217; founder Aileen Lee wrote a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2024\/01\/18\/welcome-back-to-the-unicorn-club-10-years-later\/\">long-awaited follow-up<\/a> to her original 2013 article in which she coined the term &#8220;unicorn.&#8221; The new article is illuminating on many fronts, but one line stuck with me: Of the 532 unicorns that Lee and Cowboy Ventures count in the U.S. today, there have been very few exits, with only 7% (35 companies) going public compared to 66% a decade ago.<\/p>\n<p>That means we have hundreds of unicorns in the U.S. that need to go public. The backlog is so long it would take years to clear (and we&#8217;re not even counting the hundreds of unicorns across the world). The sooner the IPO window can open, the better.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Let&#8217;s make one thing clear: Reddit going public
